## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population growth dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by the current population size P (density dependence, resource limitation, Allee effects) and possibly explicit time dependence t (seasonality, interventions/harvest, changing environment). This is typically modeled with ordinary differential equations dP/dt = f(t, P).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita rate)
- Power-law (allometric) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (nonlinear per-capita scaling with population size)
- Linear birthâ€“death with constant removal: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 (constant harvest/cull independent of P)
- Density-dependent (logistic ODE, polynomial form): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (self-limitation via crowding; carrying capacity emerges as c0/c1)
- Generalized logistic (theta-logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**(c2 + 1) (flexible curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(c2 * P)) (per-capita growth decreases ~log(P))
- Allee effect (strong Allee, cubic form): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (negative growth at low P and high P; bistability possible)
- Allee effect (factorized form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (explicit thresholds at low and high P)
- Saturating recruitment (rational inhibition): dP_dt = c0 * P / (P + c1) - c2 * P (recruitment saturates with P; losses proportional to P)
- Time-varying per-capita rate (trend): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradually improving/worsening environment)
- Time-varying density dependence: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P - c2 * P**2 (changing growth rate with fixed crowding strength)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting births/deaths)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P - c4 * P**2 (seasonality plus density limitation)
- Pulse-like intervention (smooth step in time): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * tanh(c2 * (t - c3))) * P - c4 * P**2 (policy/management shift around time c3)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If per-capita growth dP_dt / P is approximately constant over P, a linear-in-P form dP_dt = c0 * P is indicated.
- A carrying capacity shows up as a nontrivial zero of dP_dt at P > 0; polynomial forms like c0*P - c1*P**2 naturally create such a zero.
- Overcompensation/strong density dependence often requires higher-than-quadratic inhibition (e.g., dP_dt includes -P**(c+1)) to steepen decline at large P.
- Allee effects are suggested when dP_dt is negative at low P but positive at intermediate P; structurally this implies factors like P*(c2*P - 1) or a cubic with sign changes.
- A constant harvest/culling term produces a vertical shift in dP_dt (e.g., -c1) and can create extinction thresholds even if growth is otherwise positive.
- If growth rates change systematically over time independent of P, include explicit t-dependence in the per-capita rate, e.g., (c0 + c1*t)*P or exp(c0*t)*P.
- Seasonality is indicated by repeated oscillations in dP_dt over t; sinusoidal modulation of the per-capita rate (c0 + c1*sin(...))*P is a standard structure.
- Saturation of recruitment or limited reproduction at high P can be captured by rational terms like P/(P+c1), which flatten growth contributions as P increases.
- If variance increases with population size, multiplicative structures with P (or P**c) are more plausible than purely additive time-only terms.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG17)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is a **t-independent** function of **P**:
\[
f(P)=0.768873878858443\;(-1+P/8.6703748695)\,(1-P/14.3328552381)\,P\;+\;0.768873878858443\;P^{1/3}.
\]
So it is the sum of (i) a **cubic polynomial in \(P\)** (because \((-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P\) expands to a degree-3 polynomial) plus (ii) a **fractional power term** \( \propto P^{1/3}\). Any matching candidate must be able to represent a \(P^{1/3}\) term (or an exactly equal alternative form) and must not introduce any unavoidable \(t\)-dependence, logs, max-kinks, exponentials, or rational-in-\(P\) artifacts unless they can be parameter-killed to zero.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether it can be reduced (by choosing its free constants) to â€œcubic polynomial in \(P\) + constantآ·\(P^{1/3}\)â€‌ with no \(t\) dependence.

---

### 1. \(P^2 c0 + Pc1 + \frac{Pc2}{Pc3+1} + c4 + c5\log(c6(Pc7)^{c8}+1)\)
- Has a rational term \(\frac{Pc2}{Pc3+1}\) (not a polynomial unless \(c2=0\) or \(c3=0\) gives \(\frac{Pc2}{1}\) linear).
- Has a log term; to remove it set \(c5=0\).
- Even after killing log and rational (set \(c2=0\)), remaining is at most quadratic+linear+constant, **no cubic** and **no \(P^{1/3}\)**.
**No match.**

### 2. \(P^2 c0 + Pc1 + \frac{Pc2}{Pc3+1} + c4\)
- Can kill rational by \(c2=0\), leaving quadratic+linear+constant.
- Cannot produce cubic term nor \(P^{1/3}\).
**No match.**

### 3. \(P^3 c0 + Pc1 + P + c2\max(0,P+c3) + \frac{c4 t}{c5 t+c6} + \frac{c7}{c5 t+c6} + c8\)
- GT has **no \(t\)**; the \(t\)-fractions must vanish: set \(c4=0,c7=0\) (or make them constant in \(t\) is impossible for all \(t\) unless coefficients 0).
- \(\max(0,P+c3)\) is piecewise linear; to avoid kink for all \(P\), set \(c2=0\).
- Remaining is cubic + linear + \(P\) + constant. **No \(P^{1/3}\)** term.
**No match.**

### 4. \(P^3 c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{c3 t} + Pc4 + c5 e^{Pc6} + c7\)
- To remove \(t\)-dependence: set \(c2=0\) or \(c3=0\) (if \(c3=0\), term becomes linear in \(P\), still ok).
- But \(e^{Pc6}\) cannot equal \(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\); must set \(c5=0\).
- Then expression is polynomial (cubic+linear+constant), **no \(P^{1/3}\)**.
**No match.**

### 5. \(P^3 c0 + Pc1 + P + c2\max(0,P+c3) + c4 e^{c5 t} + \frac{c6}{c7 t+c8} + c9\)
- Remove \(t\)-terms: set \(c4=0,c6=0\).
- Remove max kink: set \(c2=0\).
- Left polynomial only, **no \(P^{1/3}\)**.
**No match.**

### 6. \(P^3 c0 + Pc1 + P + c2\max(0,P) + \frac{c3 t}{c4 t+c5} + \frac{c6}{c4 t+c5}\)
- Remove \(t\)-dependence: set \(c3=0,c6=0\).
- Remove max kink: set \(c2=0\).
- Left polynomial only, **no \(P^{1/3}\)**.
**No match.**

### 7. \(P^3 c0 + Pc1 + P + \frac{c2 t}{c3 t+c4} + \frac{c5}{c3 t+c4} + \max(0,P+c6)\)
- Remove \(t\)-terms: set \(c2=0,c5=0\).
- Remaining includes \(\max(0,P+c6)\) with fixed coefficient 1 (not parameterized). No way to remove it. GT is smooth (no kink).

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG17)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.7689 \cdot (-1 + P/8.670) \cdot (1 - P/14.333) \cdot P + 0.7689 \cdot P^{1/3}$$

Let me expand the polynomial part:
$$(-1 + P/8.670)(1 - P/14.333) = -1 \cdot 1 + (-1)(-P/14.333) + (P/8.670)(1) + (P/8.670)(-P/14.333)$$
$$= -1 + P/14.333 + P/8.670 - P^2/(8.670 \times 14.333)$$
$$= -1 + P(1/14.333 + 1/8.670) - P^2/124.268$$

Computing: $1/14.333 + 1/8.670 = 0.06977 + 0.11534 = 0.18511$

So multiplied by P:
$$(-1 + 0.18511P - 0.00805P^2) \cdot P = -P + 0.18511P^2 - 0.00805P^3$$

Multiplied by 0.7689:
$$-0.7689P + 0.14233P^2 - 0.006189P^3$$

So the GT is:
$$f(P) = -0.006189 P^3 + 0.14233 P^2 - 0.7689 P + 0.7689 P^{1/3}$$

**Key features of GT:**
- Contains $P^3$ term
- Contains $P^2$ term  
- Contains $P$ term
- Contains $P^{1/3}$ term (cube root)
- **No dependence on $t$**
- No Max, no log, no exp in the exact form

The $P^{1/3}$ term is crucial. This is a fractional power that cannot be replicated by polynomials, logarithms, exponentials, Max functions, or rational functions exactly.

Now let me check each candidate:

**Candidates with $t$ dependence (3-9, 11-12, 15-19, 21-22, 25-26, 29, 32):** These can potentially match if we can zero out all $t$-dependent terms. Let me check if the remaining terms after zeroing $t$ terms can match GT.

**The critical question for most candidates:** Does the candidate contain a $P^{1/3}$ (or equivalent fractional power) term? The GT requires $P^{1/3}$, which is linearly independent from polynomials, rational functions, exponentials, logs, and Max functions.

Let me systematically check:

**Candidate 1:** $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2/(Pc_3+1) + c_4 + c_5\log(c_6(Pc_7)^{c_8}+1)$
Has $\log$ term. $\log(c_6 P^{c_8} c_7^{c_8} + 1)$ â€” this is NOT equivalent to $P^{1/3}$ for any constants. The log of (power + 1) â‰  power function.
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2/(Pc_3+1) + c_4$
Polynomial + rational function. Cannot produce $P^{1/3}$.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** $P^3 c_0 + Pc_1 + P + c_2\text{Max}(0, P+c_3) + c_4 t/(c_5 t+c_6) + c_7/(c_5 t+c_6) + c_8$
Zero out $t$ terms: $P^3 c_0 + Pc_1 + P + c_2\text{Max}(0, P+c_3) + c_8$. No $P^2$ or $P^{1/3}$. Max is piecewise linear, not $P^{1/3}$.
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** $P^3 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2\exp(c_3 t) + Pc_4 + c_5\exp(Pc_6) + c_7$
Zero $t$ terms (set $c_2$ coeff appropriately, $c_3=0$ gives $Pc_2$): becomes $P^3 c_0 + P(c_1+c_2+c_4) + c_5\exp(Pc_6) + c_7$. No $P^2$ or $P^{1/3}$. $\exp(Pc_6)$ â‰  $P^{1/3}$.
Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5-50:** Following the same logic, I need to check if any candidate has both $P^2$ AND $P^{1/3}$ (or equivalent).

Let me scan for candidates with $P^2$ terms AND something that could be $P^{1/3}$:

**Candidate 10:** $P^3(c_0+c_1) + P^2 c_2 + Pc_3 + c_4\text{Max}(0,P) + c_5$. Has $P^2$ but Max(0,P) = P for Pâ‰¥0, so this is just polynomial. No $P^{1/3}$.
Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 14:** $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + P/(P+1) + P^{c_2}c_3/(P^{c_2}+c_4) + c_5 + c_6/(Pc_7+c_8)$
Has $P^{c_2}$ â€” could we set $c_2 = 1/3$? Then $P^{1/3} c_3/(P^{1/3}+c_4)$. This is a rational function of $P^{1/3}$, not $P^{1/3}$ itself. Not equivalent.
Candidate 14 verdict: [NO MATCH]

For **all remaining candidates** (5-9, 11-13, 15-50): They consist of combinations of $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$, constants, Max, log, exp, rational functions of P, and $t$-dependent terms. None contain a $P^{c}$ with free exponent $c$ that could become $P^{1/3}$, except Candidate 14 (already checked). The $P^{1/3}$ basis function is missing from all of them.
